Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This suggests that the presence of both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a specific configuration enhances the reaction yield.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interactions that enhance the reaction.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. The presence of multiple hydroxyl groups may enhance solubility or interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups might interact beneficially with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring could coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst in a favorable way.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 8: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[CX3](=O)[C;!c]'],  # Rule 9: Ketone in non-aromatic structure
        ['[c][O][C]'],  # Rule 10: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule[0])):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group
        ['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 8: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[CX3](=O)[C;!c]'],  # Rule 9: Ketone in non-aromatic structure
        ['[c][O][C]'],  # Rule 10: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule[0])):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' does not accurately capture the amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group. Consider using a pattern that captures both the amino group and the carboxylic acid group in the correct configuration, such as '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' for the amino acid and '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' for the carboxylic acid.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 2, the SMARTS pattern '[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' may not fully capture the phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid. Consider using a more specific pattern like '[c]1[c][c][c][c][c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' to ensure the aromatic ring is fully represented.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H][CX4][OX2H]' may not accurately capture sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a pattern that captures the cyclic nature and multiple hydroxyl groups, such as '[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H](=O)O'.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern '[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' may not fully capture sulfur-containing groups like thiol or sulfanyl. Consider using a pattern like '[SX2H]' for thiol groups and '[SX2]' for sulfanyl groups.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 5, the SMARTS pattern '[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1' is correct for pyridine rings, but ensure that the nitrogen is correctly positioned in the aromatic ring.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern '[NX3+](=O)[O-]' correctly captures nitro groups, but ensure that the pattern is applied to the correct context within the molecule.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' may not fully capture formyl groups on aromatic rings. Consider using '[c][CX3H]=O' with additional context to ensure it is part of an aromatic system.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)(F)' captures trifluoromethyl groups but may not capture longer fluorinated alkyl chains. Consider using a pattern like '[CX4](F)(F)(F)[CX4](F)(F)(F)' for longer chains.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern '[CX3](=O)[C;!c]' may not fully capture ketone groups in non-aromatic structures. Ensure that the pattern excludes aromatic contexts explicitly.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern '[c][O][C]' may not fully capture methoxy groups on aromatic rings. Consider using '[c][O][CH3]' to ensure the methoxy group is correctly identified.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid with carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1[c][c][c][c][c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid
        ['[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H](=O)O'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group
        ['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Nitro group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 8: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[CX3](=O)[C;!c]'],  # Rule 9: Ketone in non-aromatic structure
        ['[c][O][CH3]'],  # Rule 10: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. The presence of multiple hydroxyl groups may enhance solubility or interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups might interact beneficially with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring could coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst in a favorable way.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current validation accuracy of 0.6286 is significantly lower than the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules are not as effective in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The drop in validation accuracy indicates potential underfitting, where the model is not capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively. This could be due to the rules not being comprehensive or precise enough to capture the complexity of the data.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 5 and Rule 9 often have high positive SHAP values, indicating they might be contributing to overestimation.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 9 and Rule 10 frequently have high negative SHAP values, suggesting they might be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The significant drop in accuracy compared to previous iterations indicates that the current set of rules may not be capturing the necessary features or interactions effectively.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights that Rule 9 (ketone group in non-aromatic structures) and Rule 10 (methoxy group on aromatic rings) are frequently associated with incorrect predictions. This suggests that these rules may need refinement to better capture the nuances of their impact on catalyst loading.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 5 (Pyridine Ring):** Consider revisiting the conditions under which pyridine rings are considered beneficial. It may be necessary to incorporate additional structural or electronic factors that influence their interaction with catalysts.
   - **Rule 9 (Ketone Group):** This rule often contributes to overestimation. It may be beneficial to differentiate between different types of ketone groups or consider their position relative to other functional groups.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 9 (Ketone Group):** As it also contributes to underestimation, further investigation into the specific contexts where ketone groups are beneficial or detrimental is needed.
   - **Rule 10 (Methoxy Group):** This rule should be refined to account for the specific conditions under which methoxy groups enhance catalyst loading, possibly by considering the influence of other substituents on the aromatic ring.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce additional rules or modify existing ones to capture interactions that are currently not well-represented. This could involve incorporating more complex structural features or considering the influence of steric and electronic effects more comprehensively.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. This could involve creating new rules based on observed patterns in SHAP values or adjusting thresholds and conditions within existing rules to better align predictions with experimental outcomes.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, ultimately leading to better predictions of catalyst loading.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. The presence of multiple hydroxyl groups may enhance solubility or interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring could coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

The current rule does not account for the low yield observed with 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid, suggesting that not all sulfur groups interact beneficially with the catalyst. Consider adding sub-rules or exceptions for specific sulfur-containing structures.

Consider exploring other sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups to validate and strengthen the rule.

- **Advice 3**: For Rule 6, consider exploring additional electron-withdrawing groups beyond nitro groups to broaden the rule's applicability. This could involve testing other groups like cyano or trifluoromethyl to see if they also lead to high yields.

- **Advice 4**: Refine Rule 8 by investigating the impact of different degrees of fluorination on yield. The current rule is based on a single example, and understanding how varying the number of fluorine atoms affects the interaction with the catalyst could provide more nuanced guidance.

- **Advice 5**: Consider adding a rule or modifying existing rules to account for the influence of steric factors more explicitly. For example, Rule 11 mentions steric hindrance from long aliphatic chains, but similar considerations might apply to other bulky groups not currently covered.

- **Advice 6**: Improve Rule 10 by exploring the effect of methoxy group positioning on the aromatic ring. The current rule does not specify whether the position of the methoxy group (ortho, meta, para) affects the yield, which could be a significant factor.

- **Advice 7**: For Rule 13, consider expanding the rule to include other cyclic structures with secondary amines, as the current rule is based on a single example. This could help determine if the observed high yield is a general feature of such structures.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. This configuration may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H1+0,NX4H2+;!$([N][!C])]', '[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H][CX3;$([H1]),$([C][#6])]=[CX3]', '[OX2H][CX3;$([H1]),$([C][#6])]=[CX3]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2;$([H0]([#6X4])[c])]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[o]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[n][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3;$([H2]),$([H1][#6]),$([H0]([#6])[#6])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H1+0,NX4H2+;!$([N][!C])]', '[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H][CX3;$([H1]),$([C][#6])]=[CX3]', '[OX2H][CX3;$([H1]),$([C][#6])]=[CX3]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2;$([H0]([#6X4])[c])]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[o]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[n][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3;$([H2]),$([H1][#6]),$([H0]([#6])[#6])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. This configuration may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

ML Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy from 0.6286 to 0.6857. This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective in capturing the underlying patterns in the data. However, the test accuracy from previous iterations was higher (0.75), indicating that there might still be room for improvement.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy suggests that the model is learning better from the training data. However, the discrepancy between the validation and test accuracies in previous iterations indicates potential overfitting. The current rules might be too tailored to the training data, leading to less generalization on unseen data.

3. **Discrepancy Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 1, Rule 7, Rule 8, Rule 11) might be contributing to overestimation. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 14) might be causing underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvement Interpretation:**
   - The improvement in validation accuracy suggests that the current rules are moving in the right direction. However, the model's performance on unseen data (test set) should be monitored to ensure that these improvements are not just due to overfitting.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules (e.g., Rule 1, Rule 7, Rule 8, Rule 11) have a significant impact on the predictions. Adjusting these rules could help in reducing overestimation. Similarly, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 14) should be refined to address underestimation.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, such as Rule 1, Rule 7, Rule 8, and Rule 11, should be reviewed. Consider adding conditions or constraints to these rules to prevent overestimation.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 14, should be adjusted. This could involve relaxing some constraints or adding additional features that capture the missing interactions.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential overfitting, consider simplifying some of the rules or combining similar rules to reduce complexity. This can help improve the model's ability to generalize to new data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values (positive or negative) and evaluate their impact on both training and validation sets.

5. **Monitor Test Performance:**
   - Continuously monitor the model's performance on a separate test set to ensure that improvements in validation accuracy translate to better generalization on unseen data.

By implementing these recommendations, the rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, leading to more reliable predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

### Summary of Discussions and Directions for Optimization

1. **Effectiveness and Performance Evaluation:**
   - The current rules have shown an improvement in validation accuracy, indicating better learning from the training data. However, the test accuracy from previous iterations was higher, suggesting potential overfitting.
   - The current rules have lower train support, confidence, lift, and leverage compared to previous iterations, indicating that they might be too narrow and not capturing enough relevant cases.

2. **SHAP Analysis Insights:**
   - Certain rules (e.g., Rule 1, Rule 7, Rule 8, Rule 11) have high positive SHAP values, contributing to overestimation of modifier loading. Conversely, Rule 14 has high negative SHAP values, leading to underestimation.
   - Adjusting these rules could help in reducing overestimation and underestimation, improving the model's accuracy.

3. **Rule Specificity and Generalization:**
   - The rules might be too tailored to the training data, leading to less generalization on unseen data. Simplifying some rules or combining similar rules could help improve generalization.
   - The current SMARTS patterns for several rules may not fully capture the intended chemical structures, leading to inaccuracies in predictions.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Review and adjust rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 1, Rule 7, Rule 8, Rule 11) to prevent overestimation. Consider adding conditions or constraints to these rules.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Modify rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 14) to address underestimation. This could involve relaxing some constraints or adding additional features.

3. **Broaden Rule Conditions:**
   - Revisit rule conditions to ensure they are not too restrictive, which could help increase support by capturing a larger portion of the dataset.

4. **Refine SMARTS Patterns:**
   - Ensure that SMARTS patterns accurately represent the intended chemical structures. This may involve revising patterns to better capture specific functional groups or configurations.

5. **Iterative Refinement and Monitoring:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules, focusing on those with significant SHAP values. Continuously monitor the model's performance on a separate test set to ensure improvements translate to better generalization.

### Possibility for Further Optimization

There is potential for further optimization of the current rules without overfitting. By refining rule conditions, adjusting SMARTS patterns, and iteratively testing and monitoring performance, the rules can be improved to enhance both accuracy and generalization.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. This configuration may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

This configuration may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[o]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3v3;!$(NC=[#7,#8,#15,#16])][CX4;!$(C(N)(N)[!#6])][NX3v3;!$(NC=[#7,#8,#15,#16])]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule[0])):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. This configuration may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Matrix Checker Message:
** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])` does not accurately capture the structural description of amino acids with a secondary amino group. Consider using a SMARTS pattern that specifically targets secondary amines in amino acid structures.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS pattern `[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])` should be refined to ensure it captures phenyl groups directly attached to carboxylic or hydroxyl groups. Consider adding specific patterns for carboxylic acids and hydroxyl groups directly attached to phenyl rings.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]` may not fully capture sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a pattern that targets multiple hydroxyl groups in a sugar-like configuration.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's SMARTS pattern `[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]` should be checked to ensure it captures sulfur-containing groups like thiols or sulfanyls effectively. Consider refining the pattern to specifically target these groups.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 5, the SMARTS pattern `[n][c]` is too broad and may not specifically capture pyridine rings. Consider using a pattern that specifically targets pyridine structures.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's SMARTS pattern `[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]` should be checked to ensure it captures electron-withdrawing groups like nitro groups effectively. Consider refining the pattern to specifically target nitro groups.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern `[c][CX3H]=[OX1]` should be refined to specifically capture formyl groups attached to aromatic rings. Consider using a pattern that targets formyl groups in the correct context.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern `[CX4](F)(F)F` should be checked to ensure it captures fluorinated alkyl chains effectively. Consider refining the pattern to target longer fluorinated chains.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])` should be refined to specifically capture ketone groups in non-aromatic structures. Consider using a pattern that targets ketones in the correct context.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern `[c][OX2][c]` should be checked to ensure it captures methoxy groups on aromatic rings effectively. Consider refining the pattern to target methoxy groups in the correct context.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: For Rule 11, the SMARTS pattern `[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]` should be refined to specifically capture long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that targets longer aliphatic chains.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern `[o]1ccccc1` should be checked to ensure it captures benzofuran structures effectively. Consider refining the pattern to target benzofuran structures specifically.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `[NX3v3;!$(NC=[#7,#8,#15,#16])][CX4;!$(C(N)(N)[!#6])][NX3v3;!$(NC=[#7,#8,#15,#16])]` should be refined to specifically capture cyclic structures with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine. Consider using a pattern that targets these structures in the correct context.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern `[CX4][OX2H]` should be checked to ensure it captures hydroxyl groups on long aliphatic chains effectively. Consider refining the pattern to target these groups in the correct context.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS pattern `[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]` should be refined to specifically capture acetamido groups in combination with amino acid structures. Consider using a pattern that targets these structures in the correct context.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[o]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3v3;!$(NC=[#7,#8,#15,#16])][CX4;!$(C(N)(N)[!#6])][NX3v3;!$(NC=[#7,#8,#15,#16])]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule[0])):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H1][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3](=[OX1])[OX2H]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5
        ['[NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3](=[OX1])[#6]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[o]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3v3][CX4][NX3v3]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=[OX1])[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule[0])):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 9, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. This configuration may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid) generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid) are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown improvement in validation accuracy from 0.6286 to 0.7429. This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts. However, there is still room for improvement as the accuracy is not yet optimal.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy without a significant drop in test accuracy suggests that the model is not overfitting. However, the initial low accuracy indicates that the model might have been underfitting, which has been partially addressed in the current iteration.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 1, Rule 7, Rule 11) might be contributing to overestimation. These rules should be scrutinized for potential refinement.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 8, Rule 11) might be causing underestimation. These rules should be adjusted to better capture the characteristics of high-loading modifiers.

4. **Accuracy Improvements Interpretation:**
   - The improvement in validation accuracy suggests that the current rules are moving in the right direction. However, the presence of discrepancies indicates that further refinement is necessary to achieve better generalization and accuracy.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that contribute significantly to the prediction errors. For instance, Rule 1 and Rule 7 often have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, indicating a need for refinement.
   - Rules with consistently high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 8, should be adjusted to better account for the features of high-loading modifiers.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Rules:**
   - Rules like Rule 1 and Rule 7, which have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, should be refined. Consider revisiting the conditions under which these rules predict high loading and adjust them to reduce overestimation.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Rules:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values, such as Rule 8, should be adjusted to better capture the features of high-loading modifiers. This could involve relaxing some conditions or incorporating additional features that are indicative of high loading.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential overfitting or underfitting, consider incorporating more diverse training data or using techniques like cross-validation to ensure the model generalizes well to unseen data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently contribute to prediction errors and adjust them based on the patterns observed in the SHAP values.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or modifying existing ones to better capture the interactions between modifiers and catalysts. This could involve exploring new chemical properties or structural features that are not currently accounted for in the rules.

By following these recommendations, the rules can be refined to improve the accuracy and reliability of predictions, ultimately leading to better performance in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position and the side chain is short or contains additional functional groups like hydroxyl or phenyl (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. These configurations may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst and improve solubility.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group, especially when additional electron-donating groups are present (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid), generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure or when combined with other polar groups (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl, particularly when combined with other polar or aromatic groups (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring, especially when the pyridine is substituted with electron-donating groups (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid), often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring, especially when not combined with other electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains, particularly when the chain is long or heavily fluorinated (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid), are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure, especially when not accompanied by other functional groups that can enhance interaction (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid), generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring, particularly when combined with other electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain, especially when lacking polar or aromatic groups (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure, particularly when the structure is substituted with electron-donating groups (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid), tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with a carboxylic acid group, particularly when the amino group is in a secondary position and the side chain is short or contains additional functional groups like hydroxyl or phenyl (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid), tend to result in a high yield. These configurations may enhance coordination with the metal centers in the catalyst and improve solubility.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid or a hydroxyl group, especially when additional electron-donating groups are present (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid), generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring can provide stability and facilitate - interactions or hydrogen bonding.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure or when combined with other polar groups (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), are associated with high yields. These groups may enhance solubility and increase the interaction surface with the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group, such as thiol or sulfanyl, particularly when combined with other polar or aromatic groups (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid), tend to result in a high yield. Sulfur groups can form strong interactions with metal centers, enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring, especially when the pyridine is substituted with electron-donating groups (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid), often lead to high yields. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing catalytic activity.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro groups on an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid) can lead to high yields. These groups may influence the electronic environment of the catalyst favorably.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring, especially when not combined with other electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The formyl group may deactivate the aromatic ring or interact unfavorably with the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains, particularly when the chain is long or heavily fluorinated (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid), are associated with low yields. The high electronegativity and steric bulk of fluorine atoms might hinder effective interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a ketone group in a non-aromatic structure, especially when not accompanied by other functional groups that can enhance interaction (e.g., 4-oxoheptanedioic acid), generally lead to low yields. The ketone group might not provide beneficial interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group on an aromatic ring, particularly when combined with other electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), are associated with high yields. Methoxy groups can donate electron density, potentially stabilizing the transition state.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain, especially when lacking polar or aromatic groups (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The aliphatic chain may not interact effectively with the catalyst or could cause steric hindrance.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure, particularly when the structure is substituted with electron-donating groups (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid), tend to result in high yields. The benzofuran structure might enhance - stacking or other favorable interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure, especially when the cycle is small and rigid (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid), are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain, particularly when not combined with other polar or aromatic groups (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure, especially when the acetamido group is bulky or in a position that causes steric hindrance (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]', '[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c]', '[NX3;$([NH2][CX3]),$([NH1]([CX3])[#6]),$([N]([CX3])([#6])[#6])]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2;$([H0]([#6])[#6])]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a secondary amine in a cyclic structure, especially when the cycle is small and rigid (e.g., 1H-pyrazole-4-carboxylic acid), are associated with high yields. The cyclic structure can provide rigidity and facilitate specific interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a long aliphatic chain, particularly when not combined with other polar or aromatic groups (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The hydroxyl group may not sufficiently compensate for the lack of interaction from the long chain.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in combination with an amino acid structure, especially when the acetamido group is bulky or in a position that causes steric hindrance (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid), tend to result in low yields. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or unfavorable interactions.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]', '[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[$([OX2H]),$([OX1-])]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c]', '[NX3;$([NH2][CX3]),$([NH1]([CX3])[#6]),$([N]([CX3])([#6])[#6])]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 7
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 8
        ['[CX3;$([CX3]([#6])[#6])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 9
        ['[c][OX2;$([H0]([#6])[#6])]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 12
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 13
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10, 12]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
